<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-780192268434669570 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=780192268434669570><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/374608691191611393/630204f6cb8aaa905c4535c18bae875e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=.ruliad data-user-id=374608691191611393>Ruliad</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, November 22, 2020 7:05 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-780192268434669570>11/22/2020 7:05 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>The big appeal for Dash is if a BI tool is too inflexible for your use case. Maybe you want more user interaction or you want to build more of a data tool.

The way you would normally achieve this would be building your own UI typically with HTML,CSS and a backend server. Most Data Scientists and Data Engineers probably don&#39;t want to use these things to build dashboards. Dash abstracts away most of those elements so you can focus on quickly building with just python or R or julia. 

AKA Dash allows for a lot more flexibility in building and displaying stuff will not completely exposing having to build an UI. These means you can use whatever processing framework like spark,dask, pandas to handle the big data and use whatever visualization library you want to display it.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-783377672477605970 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=783377672477605970><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/499104423872823298/1a01884db1516a1f0a2fa9a48ed24947.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=winenose data-user-id=499104423872823298>Lauri</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, December 1, 2020 2:03 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-783377672477605970>12/1/2020 2:03 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Same brute force (with some sanity) in SQL:
<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline nohighlight">with input as (
  select explode(array(1721,979,366,299,675,1456)) as n
)
select i1.n, i2.n, i1.n * i2.n
from input i1
join input i2 on i2.n &lt; i1.n
where i1.n + i2.n = 2020</code></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, December 1, 2020 2:56 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-783461766872170516 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=783461766872170516><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/429490283848138754/aec44647c9555036c64d67cc4dc7e754.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=tylermarrs data-user-id=429490283848138754>Tyler Marrs</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, December 1, 2020 7:37 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-783461766872170516>12/1/2020 7:37 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Column level quality is simply: 
(total values – invalid count) / total values 
Be sure not to count invalid fields multiple times! 

Data set level quality is simply: 
sum(all column level quality scores) / (total columns * 100)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-783461835637915679 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=783461835637915679><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Tuesday, December 1, 2020 7:37 PM">7:37 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>You can get the stats from the Airflow DB directly.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

I wish there was more available information for interested applicants on the graduate school process. It can be intimidating.  Also, be aware that in most STEM fields, most positions will be (lowly) paid <em>and</em> include a tuition waiver. Usually the tuition waiver comes on stipulation of teaching classes or doing research credits under a grant. Also note that there are a few slightly predatory positions/labs that will not be paid and expect you to also pay $$$tuition, I would avoid these. Pay for grad students is low, but should cover room/board/fees/books at a basic level.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-786005486273167380 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=786005486273167380><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105378403699408896/6ad9a21f4adaeee654f83a08a1327a68.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=rakkit.>rakkit.</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'785980862004199455')"> Uhm, I&#39;m in healthcare. So say something is recorded as one specialty, cardiology, in the front end system.
Our service leads would say to us that if X consultant does said appointment, and it&#39;s in X appt type, then it should be a different specialty, respiratory maybe.
We have hundreds of these business rules, or changes. All different. All agreed over the years. Some still relevant. Some not. They&#39;re all just nestled into stored procedures, out of sync with eachother.
Is there a standardised way to store rules, and then apply them to my data flows between tables in SQL? </span> <span class=chatlog__reply-edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, December 8, 2020 6:28 PM">(edited)</span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(231,76,60) title=emikachi data-user-id=105378403699408896>emily</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, December 8, 2020 8:05 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-786005486273167380>12/8/2020 8:05 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>This sounds like a data mastering problem - a set of rules and definitions agreed upon by the business that may or may not change with time. Depending on how many attributes go into the rules and whether you need to preserve the history of what a rule definition was at a point in time, then perhaps these spark some ideas:
<ul><li>a mapping table that you LEFT JOIN to your data on multiple attributes</li><li>a view that you maintain over the replicated data, with a monolithic CASE statement applying all the rules</li><li>a UDF of the above monolithic CASE statement (the simple UDF should be inlined by the engine if you&#39;re running 2019, so performance shouldn&#39;t tank)</li><li>I&#39;m not familiar with the feature myself, but if you&#39;re using SQL Server Enterprise, MDS is included in that license and has a business rules feature that might fit your needs and <em>may</em> facilitate a level of self-service if done perfectly  <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/sql/master-data-services/business-rule-examples-master-data-services?view=sql-server-ver15">https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/sql/master-data-services/business-rule-examples-master-data-services?view=sql-server-ver15</a> </li></ul>(disclaimer, we recently killed off MDS where I work because it wasn&#39;t being used properly so I&#39;m hesitant to recommend this)</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, December 8, 2020 8:07 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-788156334729723924 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=788156334729723924><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105378403699408896/6ad9a21f4adaeee654f83a08a1327a68.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(231,76,60) title=emikachi data-user-id=105378403699408896>emily</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, December 14, 2020 6:31 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-788156334729723924>12/14/2020 6:31 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>not that it should constrain your design, but one example where it&#39;s great to have a dimensional model is when your reporting layer (in our case, PowerBI Pro) is in a different cloud to your data (in our case, AWS) and we don&#39;t want to get hit with a huge egress bill when we import a lot of data</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Monday, December 14, 2020 6:32 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-788157044599422987 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=788157044599422987><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, December 14, 2020 6:34 PM">6:34 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>a tall, thin fact and several wide dimensions can be a lot leaner on bandwidth and therefore refresh time and cost. Our users are mostly used to cubes so it&#39;s fine for them, though i understand a flat table might be easier for some people to grok</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-789228017675010058 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=789228017675010058><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105378403699408896/6ad9a21f4adaeee654f83a08a1327a68.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(231,76,60) title=emikachi data-user-id=105378403699408896>emily</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, December 17, 2020 5:30 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-789228017675010058>12/17/2020 5:30 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>yeah, if you have a specific set of events that you care for (date_registered, date_subscribed, date_first_order, date_closed) then accumulating is ideal since it&#39;s not very tall and will be very performant with DATEDIFF across the columns</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-789228186059538453 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=789228186059538453><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, December 17, 2020 5:31 PM">5:31 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>but inventory snapshot gives you a lot of flexibility</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-789229277836345400 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=789229277836345400><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/499104423872823298/1a01884db1516a1f0a2fa9a48ed24947.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=winenose data-user-id=499104423872823298>Lauri</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, December 17, 2020 5:35 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-789229277836345400>12/17/2020 5:35 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>In reality though it probably makes sense to just keep raw data, build some views and then figure out the aggregation scheme once things start to slow down or cost too much. Gives you time to learn as you go</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=point_up><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=☝️ src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/261d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-789536900716560405 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=789536900716560405><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/252313646682734595/eca0565bddbb2a0cf78752b7b374cb0d.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=deepak_rout>deepak_rout</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'789224280579375134')"> We want to build out a view of customer (daily view) and it will be aggreagted later over month/year ? Is there a good way to build it efficiently without strong daily records for all customers ?  Any documentations building such a time series view .. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=zachary42 data-user-id=252313646682734595>Zachary</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, December 18, 2020 1:57 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-789536900716560405>12/18/2020 1:57 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>It&#39;s generally best practice to maintain a set of the raw data down to the lowest grain somewhere. Though, I wouldn&#39;t bother with eliminating the lowest grain in your reporting database until you start experiencing disk issues and haven&#39;t tried some form of columnar compression. 

There are certain ways to make computing aggregates on different grains without the lowest grain immediately available. An example would be to store the weights of a weighted average so that you don&#39;t need the original values to compute an accurate average. You can work with a statistician, mathematician, or data scientist to come up with some of these ideas if the aggregations start to become complex. 

By default, if you&#39;re trying to deal with moving data I&#39;d recommend starting out with a type 6 slowly changing dimension / measure table across a single time axis unless you&#39;re working with multiple timelines for a data set. If your data set is large (tens of terabytes) you can consider partitioning it by yearly then monthly time grains using a date dimension key (yyyymmdd INT). If needed, you can use materialized views to do different time grain roll ups and to expose different time series (current, yearly, monthly, weekly, daily, predicted vs actual, measured vs actual, etc). 

You can compute a hash (SHA1 or higher) of the business key/s of the record and a hash of the values to do fast record compares on single columns. Hash functions are deterministic and SHA1 has 1,461,501,637,330,902,918,203,684,832,716,283,019,655,932,542,976 unique values so 2 values colliding is statistically impossible. As long as your database has a proper hash function (check your database) it should be a reliable way of computing differences. You can use windowing functions to easily compute proper time intervals for type 6 SCD if you have the timestamps as well.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-795448292376051732 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=795448292376051732><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/2.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=charts_guy data-user-id=139928557026672641>charts_guy</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, January 3, 2021 9:27 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-795448292376051732>1/3/2021 9:27 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><span class="chatlog__markdown-mention" title="rakkit.">@rakkit.</span>  it certainly would not hurt.  Especially if you have some unique projects or did something in a unique way.  If you have the code and explanations, it shows you can not only do some DE tasks, put something together, but also explain it.  Explanation is undervalued IMO as it allows you to tell the viewer exactly what is happening instead of the user having to figure it out and they might not be able to but with a little explanation you can help navigate them through it. <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-796389904900292679 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=796389904900292679><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/161154369763409921/d760257b5ffd16af7a8fa7056574cc51.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author style=color:rgb(46,204,113) title=kahnwong>kahnwong</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'796343605001322536')"> How do you deal w coworkers (from other teams) who don&#39;t seem to respond to your message , even after involving their manager </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rakkit. data-user-id=209245848960368641>rakkit.</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, January 6, 2021 11:49 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-796389904900292679>1/6/2021 11:49 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Usually I issue a response of &quot;should I not receive a response by (insert reasonable date) I will presume that this matter is closed/completed/unrequired, and as such will remove from the workload&quot;.
If asked where it&#39;s up to, why it&#39;s not done, to do it NOW because it&#39;s urgent. You have an email noting the statement that it&#39;s no longer your problem and it has to go back into the work priority queue.
Entirely political, no need to make the email sound harsh in any way, it just forces a result / blocker to be moved.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-796390560931512320 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=796390560931512320><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rakkit. data-user-id=209245848960368641>rakkit.</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, January 6, 2021 11:51 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-796390560931512320>1/6/2021 11:51 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I think encounter this a lot, and it&#39;s the only way I can forcibly move blockers that are waiting on a response that is out of my control.
Other team members have anywhere from 5-15 tasks waiting for a response, some for months and several chasing emails down the line.
At least if you can finalise something it covers your back when you&#39;ve moved onto something else and they pop back up asking for it.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-796390967178821652 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=796390967178821652><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, January 6, 2021 11:53 AM">11:53 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Sometimes people don&#39;t know what they want even when it&#39;s an urgent request, and when asked a question they don&#39;t know the answer to, it goes onto their &quot;backlog&quot; queue where it&#39;s no longer a priority to them.
Most people won&#39;t withdraw a request, from experience, they&#39;ll just ignore it if it&#39;s not forthcoming without any work by themselves.
So making that decision for them in an email helps both parties.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
